Shen Bao Wireless Weekly

Installation of Automatic Volume Leveler

— KMK

The automatic volume control in the radio is dedicated to adjusting uneven volume. Because the radio waves emitted from each broadcasting station in the sky and the stratum have different power, the sound received by the radio varies with the strength of the power, resulting in uneven highs and lows. In some cases, the power of two radio stations is the same, but the volume differs greatly. The former is because the radio itself lacks the ability to equalize and supplement, while the latter is mostly due to the quality of the environment and the proximity of the distance. This drawback of the radio is extremely annoying when listening. If receiving broadcasts from nearby or powerful radio stations, the volume feels loud, sharp, and ear-piercing, or it disturbs and obscures broadcasts from other radio stations. Conversely, when receiving broadcasts from distant or weak radio stations, the volume is too low or the disadvantage of sometimes high and sometimes low. Even if there is a volume control device, it can only avoid strong volume, but it cannot make the low volume loud. For these reasons, the radio needs to be innovated and improved in terms of volume. In the new imported radios imported into our country in recent years, almost all have this automatic volume controller, but most of them are equipped with external difference devices, while ordinary and small ones are still rare. As for what is described in this article, it is installed in an ordinary small (TRF) radio. If readers feel that the volume of the radio is uneven, they can try it according to Figure 1. Fortunately, the parts are simple to obtain, so it should not cause any difficulty.

The automatic volume leveler is achieved by combining a triode vacuum tube and several depletion resistors, because this work must be completed at the same time as detection. Therefore, a dual-screen compound vacuum tube is used for this work (see the second 55 vacuum tube in the figure), with the triode part as the automatic volume leveler and the dual screen as the half-wave detector. The line uses a self-detection method to prevent the detection work from tending to weaken. In heterodyne radios, the screen detection method is mostly used, because it is the second detection, so it is not as important as ordinary ones. As for the numerical values of other components, the attached figure has detailed instructions, so there is no need to repeat them.

Ultra-Shortwave Transceiver

— Zhi

Ultra-shortwave, what a fascinating term. Today, it is still only like a treasure trove rich in deposits, waiting for people to work hard to develop and excavate it! "Experiment" is like the only tool for excavation!

In the recent past, the Blue Hill Meteorological Observatory of Harvard University near Boston, USA, and the radio station set up by the American Amateur Radio League on a small hilltop near Hartford City, conducted two-and-a-half-meter wavelength communications. The test was successful, and the communication distance was 144 kilometers! Breaking all previous records! As for future development, it is exactly what is expected!

Comrades, based on the spirit of amateur research, mission, and hard work, let's experiment more and excavate this mysterious treasure - ultra-shortwave!

Here, two of the most affordable transceivers are introduced, willing to contribute to the comrades for reference!

The machine shown in the first figure is widely used. Two vacuum tubes are used in the machine. During reception, it acts as a detector and low-frequency amplifier. During transmission, it acts as an oscillator and amplitude modulator. Transmission and reception are managed by a four-pole double-throw switch - located at 1 to transmit, located at 2 to receive. T is a specially made low-frequency amplitude modulation dual-purpose transformer, and T is an output transformer-modulation choke.

Each coil LLr is wound with five turns of 14-gauge enameled wire with a diameter of 5 points, and L2 is wound with two turns. Capacitor C2 is a three-piece small variable capacitor. All fixed capacitors in the machine must be insulated with mica sheets. When this machine is used normally, connect a 4-foot or 8-foot long antenna to point A. A1 is used to connect a specially made Pikart (Diokord) antenna.

The network in the second figure is a relatively new transceiver. In the machine, LL1 coils are wound with 6 turns of 14-gauge enameled wire each, with a diameter of 4 points and a length of 6 points. C is an ordinary compensation capacitor, CH is a center-tapped low-impedance coil, or it can be replaced by a one-to-one low-frequency transformer in series. The high-impedance RFC is wound with 60 turns of 22-gauge double-yarn wrapped on a 3-point diameter tube.

When receiving, switch S is located at 2; when transmitting, it is located at 1.

The length of the antenna is the same as the previous machine.

The feature of this model is that during transmission, amplitude-modulated telecommunications can be listened to by the earpiece PH, without relying on other auxiliary modulators to distinguish its advantages and disadvantages.

Television and Shortwave

— Pao

Although current television has evolved from the experimental laboratory stage to the practical stage, it is actually full of obstacles and needs to be continuously tested to achieve perfection. Television sets that rely solely on mechanical action no longer have research value and have to be replaced by cathode-ray tube types. However, the television in nature - the human eye - does not need to go through the "scanning" procedure at all, and the clarity of the image and the convenience of operation are far better than current television sets. Therefore, future television will be based on a simpler new discovery, and a proper solution will be obtained, that is, the currently popular cathode-ray tube may also be abandoned.

No matter how much television will progress, it is quite possible that future television will be transmitted by shortwave radio. According to the opinions of television experts, current television sets require a 400 kHz wide band (music only requires 10 kHz) to display an image as clear as a photographic copperplate in an ordinary book. Therefore, the narrow bandwidth broadcasting band and shortwave band cannot accommodate television stations that need to occupy 400 kHz, and they have to be placed in the wide bandwidth ultra-shortwave range. However, ultra-shortwaves cannot reach far, so dozens of relay stations have to be used for retransmission; then the equipment costs of these dozens of relay stations and the special cables used for connecting the relay stations are enough to make the current television broadcast only reach a corner, and the business is difficult to prosper. Therefore, if future television can find a way to broadcast with a narrower band, then one or two powerful radio stations with a wavelength of about 20 meters will be used to avoid the need for many relay stations.

Ideal shadow, but also has sound, in order to like a sound film "sound and color" purchase in this problem is nothing more than the following three ways to solve it:

A Film and sound are broadcast together for a long time.

B The film uses the ultra-shortwave band, and the sound uses the broadcast band.

C Relatively optimal, and sound in the ultra-shortwave band, while using the same wavelength broadcast (this method has been tried successfully), then the receiver can match the same wavelength, while receiving the shadow and sound.

The Most Common Defects of Superheterodyne and TRF Radios and Their Prevention Methods

— Silian

Superheterodyne or T.R.F. (i.e., tuning radio frequency amplification) and other radios, in order to seek loud sound, the audio frequency amplification after the detection stage or the second detection stage must be performed by a pentode power tube (PoweiPentodetube), such as 2A5, 42, 41, 4347 and other vacuum tubes. This type of vacuum tube can withstand extremely high screen pressure, and its output is also extremely large. For example, the screen current output of 2A5, 42 and other vacuum tubes is 34 milliamps, so there must be a way to protect their speakers. In ordinary radios, it is often composed of an audio frequency choke and a fixed capacitor, but in superheterodyne or tuning radio frequency amplification or other devices using pentode power tubes, an output transformer is used. This type of output transformer is usually connected to an electric speaker.

The primary coil of the output voltage regulator is usually wound with 40 to 44 gauge British enameled wire, or 36 to 40 gauge American enameled wire, so it is easily burned out. If it is damp and moldy, the screen grid will easily turn red, and the music sound emitted by the electric speaker will be as thin as a mosquito's buzz, or there will be no sound at all, or even noise. After the vacuum tube suffers this huge injury, it will reduce its inherent characteristics, that is, the results after repair will always be inferior to the original clarity and loudness. This kind of defect is often encountered, so it has to be prevented. The method is to replace the primary coil with thicker enameled wire. Also, if the C resistor is damaged, this kind of defect is also likely to occur, because the control grid lacks its corresponding load. This prevention method can be to replace the C resistor with a larger watt, or not to use a C resistor and directly connect the cathode to the ground wire. If the pole soil has no corresponding load and the results are not good, the grid resistor can be changed to a megohm to two megohms.

Global Radio Statistics

— Jie Ru

The yearbook recently published by the International Radio Broadcasting Bureau shows the progress of broadcasting in various countries.

This yearbook tells us that at the end of 1934, the total number of radios in the world was approximately 48,300,000, which means that there were at least 193,000,000 listeners.

Of these 48,300,000 radios, 23,000,000 belonged to Europe, mostly with usage licenses. The United States had the largest part of this total, approximately 20,075,000, followed by the United Kingdom with approximately 6,780,560 and Germany with approximately 6,142,921. Calculated by the proportion of national population, Denmark had the most radios in the world, with an average of 160 radios per 1,000 residents.

In 1934, the total number of radios in use worldwide was approximately 3,500,000, excluding the 2 million radios in cars in the United States. This naturally increased the number of listeners by at least 13 million.

Note: L1 is wound three and three-quarters turns, with a distance of three-sixteenths of an inch between each turn; L2 is wound three-sixteenths of an inch from L1, for a total of six and three-quarters turns, close wound.

The panel is best made of aluminum, but bakelite is also acceptable. When the B power is connected to the audio frequency amplification, it should be 90 volts, but 45 volts is also acceptable, but the sound will be softer.

Publishing Industry

The Intellectual World of China Today

— Murofushi Takanobu

Japanese commentator Murofushi Takanobu recently traveled to various parts of China, both north and south, under the arrangement of Mainichi Shimbun. During his stay in Shanghai, he became known to the Chinese people for publishing his opinions on the "New Life" incident and the Sino-Japanese issue. After returning to Japan, he wrote "Travels in China" based on his travels, which were published daily in the Yomiuri Shimbun. This article is one of them. Reading it can give a glimpse of his observations on the intellectual world of China. Translator's note.

One: Hu Shih Does Not Know the Philosophy of Life Today

On the morning of the 17th, in order to exchange views with Chinese thinkers, I visited Mr. Hu Shih. Since the literary revolution, the name of Hu Shih, or Mr. Hu Shih, has been known throughout the world.

Most Japanese intellectuals probably know his name. His famous book "Outline of the History of Chinese Philosophy" has also been translated into Japanese. It has been nearly 20 years since he advocated the literary revolution, that is, vernacular literature. During this period, he has always stood on the front line of the Chinese intellectual world. Among Chinese youths, his reputation is not as good as it used to be, but he is still a first-class thinker and a leader in one field. The point of his fame is that he is the foremost in China.

Hu Shih is currently the Dean of the College of Arts at Peking University, and also edits a weekly magazine called "Independent Review." It has a circulation of 7,500 copies, which cannot be compared with the 60,000 to 70,000 copies of Shanghai's "Eastern Magazine," but it is still worthy of being the most powerful commentary magazine guiding one side of the Chinese journalistic world. If we do not mention Hu Shih, it is impossible to talk about China's academic, intellectual, commentary circles, as well as today's China and its people.

Hu Shih's home is near Peking University, at the bottom of the back door of Beiping. As soon as the car stopped in front of the door, a doorman came out to stop the dog he was raising. The courtyard inside the door is several feet wide, and the house has its own car. The house is a very grand Western-style building, which is top-notch for a scholar's life, but a little extravagant. As for me, if I were a scholar, I would have enough with eight or nine thatched huts and a life like Tao Yuanming.

After entering the door, Mr. Hu Shih, who came out from inside, led me into the guest room himself. He looked like a pale-faced scholar, of medium stature. I didn't think this was the world-renowned thinker Mr. Hu Shih.

"Mr. Murofushi," Hu Shih read, asking me for the Japanese pronunciation of this surname, and then said, "I have read Mr. Murofushi's books, but because I don't understand Japanese, I can't fully understand them."

"Sir, your name is very famous in Japan. Chiang Kai-shek, Mei Lanfang, and Hu Shih are all known to everyone in Japan."

I said politely, and he then asked: "Does Mr. still hold the ideas of Orientalism now?"

"Yes," I replied. "There is also a group of reactionary thinkers called Orientalists in Japan, but it is wrong to regard my position as the same as theirs. My Orientalism starts from the end of modern Western Europeanism and points to the future world."

"Yes," Hu Shih's expression seemed to understand and not understand. I continued to explain my position: "I belong to the category of liberalism."

"Are you not just reflecting the merchant philosophy of the capitalist era in philosophy, pragmatism, and politics, democracy?" I then asked boldly.

"I don't think so."

"I believe that so-called democracy and dictatorship are by no means absolute, immovable, or permanent truths or formulas. They are things that depend on the stage of social development and are determined by the stage of social development."

"My embrace of liberalism is not because I think everything is good, but generally it is British and American." This was Hu Shih's answer. At this point, it was impossible to reconcile.

"What about the Kuomintang?"

"The Kuomintang is not necessarily a dictatorship, and Chiang Kai-shek is certainly not a so-called dictator." His answer seemed to agree with the Kuomintang, and yet it didn't seem to agree. In short, he was against dictatorship within the Kuomintang.

From another room, he took a bound copy of "Independent Review" and a booklet he had written himself and gave them to me. He said that after reading these, I would know that China is different from Germany and Italy, and there is no need for dictatorial politics.

Later, I asked what the mainstream of the Chinese intellectual world was. He replied:

"Intellectual anarchy."

Perhaps that is so. Japan is the same. But in this state of intellectual anarchy, there is also its own direction.

We then went on to discuss the relationship between pragmatism and Bergson's philosophy, Dewey's position, Nietzsche's revival, humanism, and later on Liang Qichao. We expressed our opinions on Liang Qichao's position and the most prominent "Chinese-based culture" in today's Chinese intellectual world.

In short, Mr. Hu Shih, who was influenced by the pragmatist American philosophy, has completely not paid attention to the ideas of life that are shining in the world today.

Finally, he said: "Chen Lifu advocates vitalism, but in the end it is nothing but nihilism." This is the view of the foremost great thinker in China on the philosophy of life in the surging world.

"Do the ideas of Heidegger, Jaspers, etc. have any influence in China? But in Japan, this is the mainstream of thought," I asked. He said: "There is no influence whatsoever in China."

There is no influence in China, and there is no influence on Mr. Hu Shih, these are two different things, but the foremost great thinker in China has not paid attention to it, or at least has not thought about it enough.

(Translator's note: Martin Heidegger and Karl Jaspers are both contemporary German philosophers of life after Wilhelm Dilthey)

Two: The Scholarly Style of Empirical Research

On the evening of the 17th, I attended a banquet hosted by Mr. Tao Xisheng. Speaking of Tao Xisheng, perhaps few people in Japan know him. He is the editor of the semi-monthly magazine "Food and Goods," a professor at Peking University, and has written many books. Whether as a writer or a critic, he belongs to the first-class figures in that country. I knew his name five or six years ago. He is a new thinker, and I have read several volumes of his works.

Mr. Tao has also read a dozen volumes of my books, and seems to be able to understand my position. He sent me the bound volume of "Food and Goods" which he edited, with the words "To the Great Social Critic Mr. Murofushi Takanobu" written on the cover. I am truly overwhelmed with trepidation.

The venue was the best restaurant in Beiping. Because I was late for the agreed time, Mr. Tao had already been waiting there. Mr. Zhou Binglin, Dean of the Law School of Peking University, was also there, as was Mr. Guan Yixian, the president of "Shibao." Later came Mr. Zhang Yingnan, Professor of Administrative Law at Peking University, and Mr. Dai Xiuzan, Professor of Law. Mr. Li Da of Beiping University, is a sharp economic critic in modern China, but did not come, which is regrettable.

With a face of modesty, although he could not be compared with the late Mr. Tian Xingcun, he also had a bit of the appearance of a scholar. Unlike the talented type like Hu Shih, from his appearance, one could immediately tell that he was a sincere scholar.

We first talked about the recent intellectual world in China, and the thinking atmosphere among the youth. We also talked about communism, which once dominated the minds of Chinese intellectuals. "That was in 1924 to 1927," Mr. Tao said. "In 1927 to 1931, although it still retained its embers, it has recently been completely extinguished." Now, "Das Kapital" is no longer published. Moreover, among students, there is no trace of such a tendency."

"It is said that Beiping is a center of anti-Japanese movements..."

"That is due to internal political issues," Mr. Dai replied. Mr. Dai studied in Japan, so he understands Japanese.

"So-called internal political issues..."

"Then it is the same thing as the German National Socialist Party abolishing the Treaty of Versailles. But what about the students' recent xenophobic fervor?"

"Recently, students have been burying themselves in their studies."

"What are your thoughts on the recent North China Incident?"

"Nothing much, because we have had even more painful experiences."

This was Mr. Dai's reply. What are the "more painful experiences"? This sentence contains deep meaning. Although this sentence is not explained, it is understood throughout China. Even Japanese people, if they can understand and sympathize with the painful position of their neighbors, I think they will all understand.

Here, whether the most fundamental problem is resolved or not, people will never forget to take this into account. A great nation should be tolerant of foreign countries. Therefore, one's own self-reflection should be the most serious. We Japanese have been taught with such morality since our ancestors.

Among us, the Sino-Japanese issue naturally became the center of the topic. Because of the lack of freedom of speech, there are many obstacles, but understanding between us is easy, and in matters of understanding and agreement, everything is often resolved with very few words. Malice and conspiracy are the biggest causes of international relations falling into disputes, and only goodwill is the most effective way to resolve such disputes. What I want to say here is that the wise men of Japan and China should quickly unite.

That the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Japan handles Sino-Japanese relations, that is, diplomacy, seems to be their unanimous hope. Since the Ministry of Foreign Affairs exists, among the Japanese people, there is probably no one who does not hope for this.

The scope of our conversation ranged widely, from Lao Zhuang, the Book of Changes, the relationship between Lao Tzu and Confucius, the revival of Taoism and Confucianism. I cannot describe these here. From what I have seen, among the new Chinese thinkers, there does not yet seem to be a sufficient re-evaluation of the old Chinese learning, but no matter how new a thinker is, they are now deeply concerned about this point. At least, empirical research on the events of ancient Chinese society, and therefore on Chinese history, has become the center of academia and taste, and this is an unshakable fact.

The Japanese Common Publishing Law (Continued) (End)

— Zheng Zongkai

3. Distribution

The sale and distribution of Japanese documents and pictures are limited to merchants who are in the business of selling documents and pictures, except for authors and their heirs. Normally, distribution can begin three days after the publishing report is submitted. According to Order B No. 55 of the Ministry of Home Affairs in October of Meiji 15 (1882), the publication of portraits of shrines and temples is prohibited except by the shrines and temples themselves.

4. Restrictions on Form and Content

According to the Japanese "Publishing Law," publishers and printers of documents and pictures must include their names, addresses, and dates at the end of their documents and pictures, but the author's name is not mandatory.

Regarding the content of Japanese publications, prohibited matters, according to the "Publishing Law" and the "Juvenile Law," are listed as follows:

(1) Matters that defend crimes or offenders, or protect or reward those in criminal trials.

(2) Matters concerning preliminary examinations and litigation matters where hearings are prohibited, before public trial.

(3) Matters concerning confidential documents of diplomacy, military affairs, and other government offices, and records of government office deliberations and conference matters where hearings are prohibited, without the permission of the relevant government office.

(4) Matters that disrupt public order and harm public morals.

(5) Matters concerning military secrets, and documents and pictures without permission.

(6) Matters that undermine the political system and disrupt the national constitution.

(7) Matters concerning trials in juvenile courts and, for criminal cases involving juveniles, matters concerning their preliminary examinations and public trials.

5. Administrative Dispositions

In Japan, administrative dispositions regarding publications, according to the "Publishing Law," are of four types, which are explained separately as follows:

(1) Prohibition of sale and distribution and confiscation of engraved plates and prints. The prohibition of sale and distribution of publications is claimed by the Japanese as a unique system in their country, with few examples in other countries.

If a publication is deemed to disrupt public order or disturb public morals, the Minister of Home Affairs may prohibit its sale and distribution and may also confiscate its printing plates and prints. However, according to Article 19 of the "Publishing Law," this confiscation is limited to publications owned by the publisher or those whose business is sale and distribution; if it is already owned by an individual, it naturally cannot be confiscated.

(2) Prohibition and Confiscation of Foreign Publications. If the Japanese Minister of Home Affairs believes that publications issued in foreign countries and territories such as Korea, Taiwan, and the Kwantung Leased Territory, where the "Publishing Law" is not enforced, are detrimental to domestic public order or disrupt public morals, he may prohibit their sale and distribution within the areas where the "Publishing Law" is enforced. ( )

(3) Suspension of Magazine Publication. According to the Japanese "Publishing Law," if a magazine violates the matters it is restricted from publishing, the Minister of Home Affairs may order it to cease publication. Publications that have been subjected to a suspension of publication may not be republished under the "Publishing Law" until one year has passed.

(4) Provisional Confiscation by Prosecutors. If a Japanese prosecutor finds that the content of a publication contains prohibited matters, he may temporarily confiscate its printing plates and prints. In such cases, the parts to be confiscated and the parts not to be confiscated can be distinguished and separately divided and confiscated from the body of the printed matter.

6. Publishing Offenses

In a broad sense, a publishing offense refers to a person who violates all publishing laws and is punished. As used in this article, a publishing offense is limited to violations of the "Publishing Law." Publishing offenses can be divided into publishing criminal offenses and publishing police offenses. Publishing criminal offenses are those where the content of the publication is the basis for punishment, while publishing police offenses are those where the form of the publication is the basis for punishment.

According to the Japanese "Publishing Law," a publishing offense does not necessarily require the sale and distribution of documents and pictures; even without sale and distribution, if the purpose is sale and distribution, or if there is printing activity, the qualification for a publishing offense can be established.

In Japan, the provisions of the "Criminal Law" regarding voluntary surrender, increased punishment for repeat offenses, and combined offenses do not apply to publishing offenses. The statute of limitations for prosecution is one year.

(Note) The Japanese "Publishing Law" does not apply to Korea, Taiwan, and the Kwantung Leased Territory. These regions each have their own separate regulations: Korea has the "Korean Publishing Regulations" of the Korean Resident-General Ordinance No. 20 of Meiji 43 (1910), Taiwan has the "Taiwan Publishing Regulations" of the Taiwan Governor-General Ordinance No. 19 of Meiji 33 (1900), and the Kwantung Leased Territory has the "Kwantung Leased Territory Common Publication Handling Regulations" of the Kwantung Government Office Ordinance No. 30 of Taisho 14 (1925).

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

The Global Trend of Restoration

— Meng Ruo

Strangely enough, the recent global trend of restoration has surged so powerfully. One moment Greece is shouting for restoration, the next Austria is also clamoring for it, as if restoration has become a fashionable political movement. It exhausts a group of deposed emperors, princes, and aristocratic royalists, who are extremely busy preparing to come out and take action to restore their former lost empires. Although these two European restoration movements have currently subsided because the time is not yet ripe, their restorationists are already celebrating each other in anticipation, waiting for the arrival of an unexpected opportunity to fulfill their long-cherished ambitions.

Naturally, as long as they are not idiots, emperors and nobles would want to enjoy their lifestyle. Many Luzon people stranded on the Huangpu River in Shanghai, although now living a pitiful life of begging in a foreign land, cannot help but want to immediately overthrow the Soviet government when they think of their past glory and wealth. The White Russian restoration movement may also be launched in the future.

Look, today a Turkish prince, because his great ambition for restoration failed, committed suicide in indignation. A Reuters New York dispatch reported: A young man committed suicide in a hotel here, and it is now known to be Klin, the grandson of the former Turkish Emperor Hamid, aged thirty. According to a letter left to the police chief here, the reason for the suicide was his infatuation with a wealthy American woman who owned a huge inheritance. He had planned to marry her so that he could use her wealth to recruit and train an army to return to his country and carry out a restoration. However, good things are often difficult, and the marriage did not materialize. In despair, he took this drastic measure.

The recent prevalence of the global trend of restoration is indeed a good ornament to the turbulent situation. Generally, the occurrence of restoration movements is due to the machinations of a group of evildoers. But if there is no environment to create restoration, the evildoers will have no way to act. For example, the current restoration in Austria is promoted by the power struggle between Italy and Germany.

Lament on Lake Tai

— Li Ang

Lake Tai, always so tranquil, like a gentle face, even when there is a windy day, the rolling green waves, following the wind, gradually pass by, without containing any danger. The continuous mountain ridges, the near ones are emerald green, the far ones are light purple, and the places where stones have been excavated appear tiger yellow, like jade inlaid with coral. The sky, like a piece of azure velvet, sets off the scene with extraordinary clarity.

Tranquil and clear Lake Tai, immersed in such radiant and beautiful gemstones: emerald green and light purple...

Another gemstone rolled up from the lake water—

In the morning, the reeds, covered in water dew, were whispering in the wind, the sparrows were chattering noisily on the willow branches of the stone embankment, and the eastern sky was undergoing an extraordinary transformation. When those long strips, long strips of rainbow, resembling the color of accumulated blood, spread out, an early sun, like a round, transparent amber ball, gradually, gradually, rose above the horizon. Then, every blade of grass, every leaf, every flower... on the earth was splashed with the brilliance of life, and the ducks also flocked to the beach to find food.

On such a morning, treading on the water dew on the grass, I prepared to go to the stone pond to see an old relative who was ill. By nature, I was afraid of seeing the twilight, afraid of seeing an elderly person who was dying. However, having received the instructions of my elders, I could not escape and had to go early once. At this time, the small steamer had not yet arrived, and I hired a ferry at Baojie Bridge.

I sat obliquely on the bow of the boat, and the woman rowing the oar at the stern was about thirty years old. The boat slowly parted the short reeds and rippled towards the lake surface. The amber sunlight shone on my face and also shone on her face. I was melancholy, thinking of an elderly person who was dying, but she also looked so melancholy, what was she thinking of? Yes, I remembered what she had said to me just now:

"Sir: Are you going to the stone pond? It's sixty cents for a round trip."

Her voice was trembling and hoarse, like the sound of a loose bowstring, with a hint of lament. I began to suspect that she had quarreled with her husband, or had been abused by her parents-in-law for no reason? Because, in rural families, this is very common, the more difficult life is, the easier it is for a daughter-in-law to be wronged... I kept thinking like this, watching the retreating gray and white long bridge. The woman at the stern sighed as she looked at me. The oar in her hand seemed about to be put down, but I didn't want to say a word to her, "What unpleasant things do you have, can't you row faster?" These words reached my throat and then slipped back into my stomach.

Why, on this lake surface in the brilliance of life, was there a boat full of dark melancholy!

"Rower, is this the only boat your family has?" I finally started talking to her.

"There is only one, I don't row when my man is here." Her eyes were red, the sunlight turned white, scorching hot on my neck, scorching on her withered yellow hair.

"Then how did he die?"

"He died of illness, he had typhoid fever the month before last!"

"How old was he?"

"Only twenty-five, alas... he didn't even celebrate his birthday."

"Aren't you yourself about thirty years old!" I was surprised by their mismatched ages.

"Oh, no, it's just that I've been worn down like this, sir: The whole burden is on my shoulders, a two-year-old child at home, a paralyzed grandfather, and the grandmother is also like the setting sun!"... Saying this, she suddenly stopped, and her haggard face turned to face the emerald green mountain ridges. She seemed to regret that she shouldn't have talked about her family affairs in front of an unrelated person. She rowed the oar a little faster. I dared not mention anything to her again.

The boat, facing the morning breeze, rippled forward, the rolling green waves of the lake, were so tranquil and yet so gentle, I held back my sigh, letting the reeds frequently shake their heads at me, and the fishing nets frequently shed tears for me.

Three Pagodas of Dali

— Dan Er

Dali, nestled in the embrace of the secluded and expansive Cangshan Mountains and the gentle and light Erhai Lake, possesses uniquely outstanding scenery in all seasons:

"Wind, flowers, snow, moon."

The whole of Dali is intoxicated, like an ethereal and exquisite beauty, swaying in dance, making the people under Cangshan feel almost like they are about to ascend into the heavens. But on hot summer nights, Dali is uniquely the best season. The scenery and atmosphere of summer nights often make tourists feel as if they are in a dream.

The evening breeze rises, and the trees on Cangshan play a more rustling and leisurely melody. The Erhai Lake, with its mirror-like blue waves, ripples and undulates. People already feel as light as if they were in the cool ninth month of autumn, exceptionally refreshing. Strolling near the foot of Cangshan and climbing Cangshan, bursts of clear, serene, and fragrant air permeate the heart and spleen, making one feel comfortable even in the bones, floating and looking at the secluded, winding, and fascinating mountains and clouds, like a person from another world. Stopping under the dense shade, the cool breeze gently brushes the sleeves, clear, ethereal, and moistening, making one feel as if they have suddenly grown several times taller. The tranquility is so intoxicating that one feels lost and without a master, body and mind merged into nature, no longer

Page 20

in the human world. I love to linger and hesitate, the beauty of the mountains is deep, the sky is clear and pure white, the body and mind are light, heaven and earth, a seamless whole. It is often said that the wind disappears in the sleeves, I think only at this time can one have that kind of realm to speak of.

The summit of Cangshan is covered with snow all year round, but the climate is like spring in all seasons. The white snow is like white snow, shrouding the mountains, extraordinarily beautiful, making people gaze endlessly. The strong may even bravely climb the mountains to play in the snow, their laughter loud and clear, often heard from the secluded valleys, faintly distinguishable, extremely tempting, feeling both illusory and delicate, seeming near and far. If you raise your eyes while holding a tree and look down at Cangshan, it is like a quiet and indistinct painting, a night scene of unparalleled beauty, making it impossible to tell where is the most wonderful or the most beautiful.

Slowly stopping the trembling soul, carefully examining. From the quiet, misty, and lush area, a huge pen rack emerges faintly, like a celestial being slowly descending from the sky. Even in the night, under the clear and pure white air, it is simple, pure white, and steadfastly gazing. That kind of towering and majestic spirit shakes the heart. This is the most magnificent Three Pagodas of Dali. Then, continuing south, vaguely and distantly, another giant pen suddenly stands erect, seemingly connected to the sky. Looking back at the Three Pagodas, they look like a giant and beautiful pen rack, firmly holding a pen beside them. Amidst the ceaseless amazement, one will also find the uniquely elegant Jade Wave Pool in front of the Three Pagodas, near the seaside, its lush green water seems to be overflowing. At this time, one will suddenly feel as if in another world, as if oneself is an artist, with a stunning landscape painting spread out in front, the Three Pagodas are a pen rack, the other spire is a paintbrush, and the Jade Wave Pool is an ink pot. Scenery, people, pagodas, and paintings are all merged into one. Gazing in awe:

"What an exquisite picture!"

How the magnificent Three Pagodas were created, no one knows, and how big and how tall they are, there is no way to understand. To look up at the spire under the pagoda, one must raise one's head so high that the hat falls off and still not see clearly. It is best to lie down on the ground and look up at the sky. The pagoda body is about eighteen stories high, and each story is very tall. The size of the pagoda body requires one hundred and twenty-four people to reach out and surround it, which shows its enormous scale. Each story spirals upwards, and the strongest person can only climb to the sixth story before being unable to withstand the strong wind. Therefore, from this point, one can also guess the pagoda's extraordinary height. At the very top of the spire are five giant iron gourds, the ones above getting smaller, and one year a hurricane blew down the last one. Seen from the ground, it was so tiny that it could not be seen, but when it appeared on the ground, it was a huge iron object that several people could not drag, several feet high, larger than a square table. Below the gourd is a cluster of iron trees, and a small branch once fell off, but when it landed on the ground, it was larger than a coffin. Further down are several golden chickens, and once a piece of a golden chicken foot collapsed, as big as a huge gourd. This made the people of Dali see it as a mysterious and magnificent pagoda. The magnificent and enormous scale of the construction shows that China had astonishing achievements in ancient times, but this is rarely known to people.

Looking at this exquisite picture, and thinking of the magnificence of the giant pagoda forgotten by the people of the country, one is filled with amazement that seems both tragic and poignant. Looking around again, the mountains, the pagodas, and the people seem to tremble, almost making me fall off the mountain. Ah! What admirable "scenery"!

Commercialized Schools!

Kidnapped (Part 2)

— Lin Hao

"Softer, softer! There are bandits!" The old master lowered his hoarse voice to almost nothing! As if he had a huge burden on his shoulders.

Everyone was quietly silent, only the sound of heavy breathing could be heard.

"Bang, bang, bang" there was another burst of urgent gunfire, and the old master was clearly alarmed, his face revealing infinite sorrow.

Gently, we stepped out of the gate, one step at a time.

A large group of black shadows came into view: The old master said in a trembling voice, "Who is it?"

As they approached, we realized that it was the local militia: "Where are the bandits?"

"Over there:" The old master pointed to the distant clumps of trees. (Behind the trees was a large pile of black mountains.)

The militia first turned their gaze over there and stared for a few moments, then took down the flintlocks on their backs and crept forward, step by step.

It was as solemn as if it would always be silent here.

After a while, the gunfire over there became even more urgent, and it was clear that they were engaged in a firefight. Everyone held a special hope, praying.

The night was spent in a terrifying situation.

The next day, large groups of people gathered in the inn, talking about the events of last night: "Hey, those bandits were really fierce! When they couldn't kidnap the child, they shot and knocked down Jin Sangui. Then they carried the child away, but they were surrounded by the militiamen! They then went at it with 'bang, bang, bang.' Hmph, the result is something that no one would believe!..."

"How so?"

"The child was finally kidnapped!" Disappointed large eyes.

I had no mood to bother with this idle account; I jumped onto the mule cart: The coachman cracked the whip loudly on the mule's back, and the cart gradually turned towards the road bathed in the faint morning light.

Dawn

— Hua Mu

Before dawn, the mind and spirit return to a state of tranquility and clarity. I remember in my childhood, I followed this belief, and when the eastern sky broke light, I would squat on the steps of the sky and read aloud the books that the teacher taught me, the diligent and earnest situation, now when I think of it, it seems like it is before my eyes. However, this kind of realm is only something that children in the countryside can enjoy, like in Shanghai, habits and environment have pushed the morning back to eight or nine o'clock.

I can't help but thank this ordinary living environment, which has allowed me to break away from the urban residence of Shanghai and go to this semi-rural town of Jiangwan, and allowed me to see again before dawn my tranquil heart and clear unified spirit. Although the increase in age has no longer retained that narrow realm of childhood, but because of the experience of life, I have seen here the beautiful and ugly realities of various states.

After a moderate sleep, I gently woke up from my dream again. Half a blanket covered my peaceful limbs. The world at this time is enough to plunge one into the sea of thought. Outside the window, the sky is quietly hazy, the sparse stars are sleepy: Outside the fence, the dark shadow of a sycamore tree is dotted there. The sound of frogs, crickets, and the long chirping of earthworms come from the fields in the distance, showing the peace and tranquility of the earth. The eastern sky is gradually turning white. The short and powerful crowing of a rooster seems to have lost the distant charm of the loud crowing at noon, this small animal, perhaps to welcome the coming of light, its pulse is excited.

The sirens of the factories in Zhabei have gradually begun to sound loudly, this heavy signal, from far to near, breaks through the tranquil air, and seems to vibrate the sleeping bed. How many people, carrying sweat and fatigue, are spit out from that iron gate, and how many people, with anemic hands and faces, begin to be swallowed in from the iron gate. These kinds of associations stimulate my brain and gradually make me uneasy. At this time, the sharp cries of crows respond to the factory sirens, the atmosphere becomes even more solemn and tense, this mixed sound wave covers up the clear and wonderful wing strings of the crickets outside the fence, and the chanting of the earthworms. The nerves have been besieged in an atmosphere of bewilderment and sorrow. This animal also realizes that the iron shackles of life are about to be placed on people's backs again. For the sake of life, humans and animals must both suffer.

Another burst of rooster crowing. Earth-shattering trucks, madly speeding past the road outside the fence. Dogs bark, greeting the vegetable vendors driving to the market. Listening to these cries of sorrow squeezed out for life, one cannot help but think of the vegetable growers in their hometown, year after year, they also carry vegetables from before dawn to the city market, exchanging them for a day's worth of rice that is barely enough to fill their stomachs; they also have to bear countless miscellaneous donations and taxes. Life has pressed them so much that they can't even squeeze out a sigh when hurrying on the road.

The noise of the city streets is stirring up, how many treacherous merchants are again beginning to swindle and contend with those honest villagers. Between people there is always a cruel divide! The wing strings of the crickets are cut off sometime, and a few stars have also fallen asleep. The butcherbirds in the garden have already begun to sing loudly their sinister laughter, singing with abandon; alarming the sleeping sparrows, chirping and jumping on the telephone wires, innocently saying good morning to this newly awakened earth. The handcarts squeak and groan. Afterwards, the first train on the Songhu line also raises its childish voice and slides away at full speed. The fog over the fields gradually dissipates. In the sound of the early cicadas, draped in a morning gown, leaning on the window railing, watching the bright red sunrise, slowly spitting out fierce golden arrows, shooting towards my face. Suddenly, I feel a surge of inner encouragement!

The earth has completely awakened. Light repeats its illumination across the human world. Humanity must again shed sweat and blood for the sake of light!

"Preface to Liu Xiang's 'Strategies of the Warring States'" (6)

However, the state of Qin had the advantage of geography and profit. The strategists all rushed to it first. Su Qin initially wanted to ally with Qin, but Qin did not employ him, so he allied with the eastern states. Therefore, the First Emperor, relying on a country surrounded by strongholds, and the obstructions of Hangu Pass, and the benefits of Long and Shu, listened to the strategies of many people, and taking advantage of the legacy of the Second Emperor, he nibbled away at the six states, annexed the feudal lords, and possessed the empire. He relied on criminal law as governance, and trusted small tricks as the way, so he burned books and buried scholars alive. He looked down on Yao and Shun, and disdained the Three Kings. The Second Emperor was even worse, with no grace descending, no feelings reaching, the ruler and his ministers suspecting each other, and blood relatives becoming estranged. The transformation of morality was shallow and weak, the norms of governance were destroyed, and the people did not see righteousness and hung on to unrest. He ruled the empire for fourteen years, and the empire collapsed greatly. This was the evil of deceit and falsehood. How far it was from the virtue of a king!

Don't Let It Down

— Little Angel

The lack of universal Chinese children's education and the severe deficiency in Chinese children's education represent a tremendous loss for China and all its children. Indeed, children's education is the foundation of the nation's education, and its importance cannot be overstated.

Given the hardships and difficulties in China today, the future responsibilities of children are particularly significant. To enable these children to shoulder these arduous and significant future burdens, it is imperative to actively cultivate and nurture them, fostering a resilient strength within them. We believe that the primary factor in developing this strength is undoubtedly the provision of a positive environment.

Tragically, a considerable number of Chinese children are being harmed by fundamentally irrational living conditions. If we were to witness the film "Little Angel," we would undoubtedly experience a profoundly stimulating effect.

Indeed, the environment of children is certainly not created by the children themselves. However, who should be responsible for changing their environment?

We believe that the screening of "Little Angel" will cause countless parents to shed tears of shame, while simultaneously saving the souls of numerous children.

The appearance of "Little Angel," a film drama imbued with the essence of children's education, on the Chinese film scene today represents an exceptionally valuable contribution. For the sake of China and its children, we naturally hope that the entire film industry will continue to work hard on this.

Finally, I would like to say: "Little Angel" was produced for families with children, and families with children should not let it down!

Star's New Films Released

(3) "Night Fragrance," directed by Cheng Bugao, stars Hu Die, Zhao Dan, and Shu embroidery Wen. It depicts the various misfortunes of a flower girl (played by Hu Die) who is lured by vanity. The plot is extremely tortuous and sorrowful, showcasing Hu Die's elaborate work after returning to China.

(3) "Jade Horse," directed by Xu Xinfu, stars Wang Zhengxin, Ji Jianong, Yan Yuexian, and Gu Lanrong, with the anti-drug movement as its theme. The film features grand sets, such as bizarre and winding secret rooms and tunnels, and magnificent and luxurious new-style buildings. The whole film is full of tension and terror. Reviewers know that directing martial arts detective films is Xu's forte.

(4) "Boatman's Daughter," directed by Shen Xiling, stars Gao Zhanfei, Xu Lai, Sun Min, and others. Lao Gao plays a worker here, which is perfect for his personality. In "Boatman's Daughter," he clearly achieves amazing results. Xu Lai, Sun Min, and others also display a variety of emotions. Director Shen Xiling is praised as the director who "understands film" the most, and here, he has achieved even greater success than "Nostalgia."

The five films that are in the planning stage and awaiting production are as follows:

(1) "Peach Blossoms After the Calamity" will be directed by Zhang Shichuan and star Hu Die and Gao Zhanfei. The script is by Hong Shen (originally published in literature). (2) "Brothers' Journey" is Zheng Zhengqiu's unfinished work "He Died Before He Could Succeed," which will now be co-directed by Cheng Bugao and Zheng Xiaoqiu, starring Hu Die, Gao Zhanfei, and others. (2) "Love Letter" will be written and directed by Li Pingqian, with Hu Die, Gao Zhanfei, and Ye Qiuxin already chosen as the main cast. (4) "Spring Flower" will be written and directed by Wu Cun, with Gao Zhanfei already confirmed for the main cast, and possibly the entire cast of "Remarriage." (5) "New People, Old People" will be directed by Cheng Bugao, with the main cast yet to be determined. All of the above are sound films.

Yuan Meiyun and Child Star Liu in "Victory Song"

Publishing World

Since its publication, Ying Wu News has been deeply welcomed by people in the film and dance circles because of its well-informed news and many gimmicks. It is reported that the sixth issue has now been published, with many wonderful articles such as "A Eulogy for Dancing Star Li Meimei" and "One of Yuan Meiyun's Foster Brothers"... all of which are rare gems. In addition, a flower news column has been specially opened to publish anecdotes and love histories from the flower world. This issue is particularly rich, and the dance star trailer registration has been published in succession since the last issue. There is also an article about the scandalous history of the three dance queen sisters, which will be published in the next issue.
